You‚Äôll get to experience the nature, water, breathtaking views of the Bay and best of all completely be able to explore this entire island on foot or on bicycle( highly recommended).

< Text>
Very cool island! Angel island was apparently the Ellis island of the west and processed/quarantined Asian immigrants. It was also a military base. There‚Äôs old abandoned buildings that you can explore everywhere - very eerie and awesome!

We did the ring home that circles the island and it took us about 4 hrs walking at a moderate pace. Ferry is a little pricey (~$20 round trip) but it‚Äôs a nice day trip.

There‚Äôs also a cute cafe on the island with salads, sandwiches and beers but you could also bring your own picnic.</Text>

<text>Camping on Angel Island is a must on the bucket list. Take the effort to book a campsite six months in advance. Awesome views of East Bay and SF all around, a surreal escape from the city jungle. A night hike up to MT. Livermore will be rewarded with stars and city lights.<//text>< pics>

Beautiful state park. Great place to hike or bike. Be sure to visit the immigration station. I learned a lot about the Chinese Exclusion Act and how Angel Island, unlike Ellis Island, was not a very welcoming place for Asian immigrants. Very interesting experience.</review>

< review>
Wow! What a gem! Loved the island. We rented bikes on the mainland at Pedego Bikes and brought them over on the ferry.

Had a blast riding on the lower loop road. There are non-stop views all over the island. Saw Alcatraz, Golden Gate Bridge, downtown, it was great.

We had no idea about all the military and immigration history here that was fascinating to learn about. Nice signs all over the island in its various sections< /review>

<Text>Had a camp site on the East Bay site #3 for the night. Highly recommend. More protection from the ocean wind and great views of East Bay and part of downtown SF. There is a faint beep from a buoy on that side but you come to ignore it after a while. Lots of deer, turkey vultures, red tailed hawks, and the occasional raccoon at night. Keep food in the lock box as the raccoons are brave.
The hikes are really easy and surprisingly quick to get around. Mount Livermore is beautiful with 360 degree views. The map is pretty spot on and the park rangers are all super friendly. It's a must for everyone, whether you live in the city or not. Book your campsite 6 months in advance to beat the rush!</Text>< Pictures>

<user_name>Travis Shaw< /user_name><date>1519532035240</date><rating>5<//rating>< Text>
Angel Island is a wonderful place to visit.  I recommend taking the earliest ferry available to be one of the first in the island.  Blue and Gold Fleet offers a 9:45am departure that gets you there around 10:15am.  It will take about 2 hours to summit Mt. Livermore and return.  On weekdays there is a Ferry that leaves the island at 1:50pm and another at  3:40pm.  The weekend is less ideal with 12:30pm and 4:15pm ferry pick-ups from the island.  It makes perfect sense to stay longer if you‚Äôve brought a lunch or plant to eat at the cantina (seasonally open).  Return ferries also take a bit longer (usually) as they often stop in Tiburon and Sausalito.  Bring a bike to Angel Island is a great way to squeeze in a visit to the entire island if you plan to make it a single day trip.  They also let bikes board the ferry first, so you‚Äôll have your pick of the best seating!  The island itself is breathtaking and has quite possibly the best views of the bay that are possible from land.</Text>

108960145475661836825</user_id>
<text>Angel Island is an island in San Francisco Bay offering expansive 360¬∞ views of the San Francisco skyline, the Marin County Headlands and Mount Tamalpais. The entire island is included within Angel Island State Park and is administered by California State Parks. The island, a California Historical Landmark,[1] has been used for a variety of purposes, including military forts, a US Public Health Service Quarantine Station, and a US Bureau of Immigration inspection and detention facility. The Angel Island Immigration Station on the northeast corner of the island, where officials detained, inspected, and examined approximately one million immigrants, has been designated a National Historic Landmark.Angel Island is the second largest island in area of the San Francisco Bay (Alameda is the largest). The island is so large that on a clear day, Sonoma and Napa can be seen from the north side of the island; San Jose can be seen from the south side of the island. The highest point on the island, almost exactly at its center, is Mount Caroline Livermore, more commonly known as simply Mt Livermore, at a height of 788 feet (240 m). The island is almost entirely in the city of Tiburon, in Marin County, although, there is a small sliver (0.7%) at the eastern end of it (Fort McDowell) which extends into the territory of the City and County of San Francisco. The island is separated from the mainland of Marin County by Raccoon Strait, the depth of the water approximately 90 feet. The United States Census Bureau reported a land area of 3.107 km¬≤ (1.2 sq mi) and a population of 57 people as of the 2000 census<//text>< Time>
1526543589057< /Time>

< review>
It's pretty cute and cozy park. There are plenty benches and there two covered gazebos with tables. I love the ambience here, very romantic. Unfortunately, there's no parking and there is no fence to ensure the kids safety. There is a vast green open space to run after your kid if they decide to run towards the street, but I must say it's nerve wracking that the park is built right on a main street  with lots of traffic. I wish it would have a fence. Other than that, beautiful.</review>

<review>My wife and I started coming here in late May and loved the place so much that we have come back almost every single week since, sometimes twice a week!

The wine and beer are both good, all local San Diego county breweries and wineries. But the best part, the guys pouring the drinks. We were introduced to the bartender, Joe, on our first visit. He was so awesome that we knew we had to keep coming back. His knowledge of wine is second to none. He is a professionally trained sommelier and oh man does he know his stuff. I have learned more about wine than I ever thought possible. He has such a great passion for what he does and it really shows. A few months later we were introduced to Colton, another great personality and fun person to be around.
